## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science – mechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task captures the stress–strain response of a material at different temperatures, a central problem in plasticity and thermo-mechanical behavior of metals. Stress typically depends on strain through hardening laws and on temperature through thermal softening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic regime, small strains)
- Hollomon power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (monotonic plastic flow without yield offset)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield strength followed by power-law hardening)
- Voce saturation hardening: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(-c2 * epsilon) (hardening that saturates at a maximum stress)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (c1 + epsilon)**c2 (power-law with pre-strain or offset strain)
- Linear thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T) (separable temperature reduction factor)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(-c2 * T) (thermally activated decrease of flow stress)
- Temperature-dependent hardening exponent: sigma = c0 * epsilon**(c1 + c2 * T) (hardening rate that varies linearly with temperature)
- Quadratic flow curve with exponential thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2) * exp(-c3 * T)
- Power-law with critical temperature: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - T)**c3 (softening toward a critical temperature, e.g. melting)
- Saturation hardening with linear thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) * (1 - c2 * T)
- Double power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 + c2 * epsilon**c3 (two-stage strain hardening)
- Yield strength linear thermal softening plus hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - c1 * T) + c2 * epsilon**c3
- Saturation strain hardening with power-law exponent: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon**c2)) * exp(-c3 * T)
- Linear plus power-law hardening with thermal factor: sigma = (c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T)
- Creep-inspired hyperbolic sine with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon) * exp(-c2 * T) (flow stress for high-temperature deformation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear loading at small strains → additive linear term c*epsilon indicates elastic regime.
- Non-zero stress at zero strain → additive constant c0 captures initial yield strength.
- Strain hardening that gradually saturates → exponential decay term (c0 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) models approach to a saturation stress.
- Power-law sub-linear growth → epsilon**c with c < 1 typical of dislocation-based plasticity.
- Thermal softening reduces strength monotonically → multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or exp(-c*T) decreases stress as T rises.
- Strong temperature sensitivity of flow stress → exponential Arrhenius-like factor exp(-c/T) or exp(-c*T) dominates the T-dependence (similar to pre-built forms, but can be combined with other terms).
- Temperature-dependent hardening rate → power exponent containing T, e.g., epsilon**(c1 + c2*T), reflects thermally activated recovery.
- Strength drops toward zero near a critical temperature → term (Tm - T)**n or (c2 - T)**n gives vanishing stress at the limit.
- Multiple hardening mechanisms → sum of two or more terms with distinct exponents (e.g., c1*epsilon**n1 + c2*epsilon**n2) suggests different obstacle populations.
- Offset strain before hardening → (c1 + epsilon)**c2 form or Swift law indicates a pre-strain or threshold strain for plastic flow.
